Activities of the French in Yunnan Province 94

｜Impressions of a U.S. Reporter's Visit to Yunnan｜

Mr. Burden, a correspondent for the *New York Sun* in China, recently traveled to Yunnan to investigate the activities of the French in the province. He wrote an article about his observations, which was published in the *New York Current Affairs Monthly*. We are translating it below for reference:

Regarding the Chinese side, there is an understanding regarding the spheres of influence of France and Japan in their activities in China. This idea has drawn attention to France's Far Eastern empire. France's power in the Far East, apart from the Guangzhou Bay leased territory and small concessions in Tianjin, Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Hankou, is concentrated in Indochina. It holds special interests in Yunnan Province in southwest China, a place rarely visited by foreigners. The French do not deny this. In recent months, Chinese critics have felt that Japan's actions in Manchuria have upset the balance of power among the powers in China, which is bound to provoke reactions from other parties. Therefore, there is talk of France occupying Yunnan. This claim is based not only on the belief that there is an understanding between France and Japan regarding the partition of China but also on the fact that France's activities in Yunnan have clearly increased.

The correspondent (as the author calls himself), in view of the widespread nature of these rumors, traveled to Yunnan to conduct an on-site investigation of the situation of French activities. After the investigation, he felt that there were no signs that France was planning to drastically change its current policy. However, he did find that its monopolistic control in Yunnan Province had clearly increased.

The most convenient external transportation route for Yunnan Province is a single railway line, which passes through Indochina and is owned and managed by the French. The railway runs from Haiphong on the Gulf of Tonkin, through Hanoi, the capital of Indochina, to the provincial capital of Yunnan. Although the entire line is only a little over 530 miles long, the 288-mile section through Yunnan is mountainous, rugged, and steep. It is about 250 feet above sea level at the Yunnan-Vietnam border and rises to 6,400 feet in Yunnanfu (Kunming). There are no particularly fast trains on this line, and because there are many bandits in the mountains, it is closed at night. It takes three days to travel from Hanoi to Yunnanfu.

Except for a few areas, the entire province of Yunnan is mountainous. Most of the province is located on the Himalayan plateau, which includes Tibet and most of Sichuan Province. Some of its peaks rise to 22,000 feet above sea level. For this reason, it rarely interacts with other parts of China.

Only small boats can navigate the Yangtze River on the northern border of Yunnan Province. It takes 23 days to travel by camel from Yunnanfu to Xufu, and then at least six weeks to reach Shanghai by water, with many stops along the way.

There is another route, which involves traveling by camel from the provincial capital to Mengzi, then taking a train to Nanning in Guangxi Province, and then traveling by water along the West River to Guangzhou, which takes about a month. Conversely, it takes less than a week to travel from Guangzhou to Yunnanfu via Haiphong, and only ten days from Shanghai to Yunnanfu via Haiphong. Furthermore, traveling by camel caravan is quite expensive and is only suitable for transporting opium.

Years ago, there was talk of building a Yunnan-Burma railway, but the British side has not yet challenged French power by implementing this plan. There have been no recent proposals, so France's control of the gateway to Yunnan is unchallenged. Goods sealed in Indochina are not allowed by the French. Therefore, all goods shipped to Yunnan must be inspected by French customs in Haiphong. All travelers entering and leaving Yunnan Province must, of course, obtain French passports. Although, to my knowledge, such passports have never been refused to Europeans or Orientals, travelers are subject to close surveillance.

The transportation of goods is often prohibited. Any weapons or ammunition from non-French sources cannot enter Yunnan Province via Tonkin. Even military supplies from French sources cannot be shipped without special permission from the French authorities. However, it goes without saying that a government friendly to France can easily obtain the military supplies it needs. When I was in Yunnanfu, a shipment of munitions worth US$1.45 million arrived, which is about 60% of the province's budgeted revenue. It may also be noted that the French classify radio receivers and transmitters as military supplies and prohibit them from being shipped into Yunnan Province via Indochina, even if they come from French sources. When I was in Yunnanfu, I saw a set of equipment that a Chinese person had brought in from Shanghai via Xufu. The transportation cost was exactly equal to the selling price of the equipment in Shanghai. Any item used to manufacture munitions must be specially licensed to be shipped from Tonkin. For example, the British hospital in Yunnanfu must obtain permission from the French consul stationed there before it can import various necessary acids.

Airplanes are also classified as military supplies. In 1932, six American aircraft purchased by the Yunnan government were refused shipment. After protests from the U.S. State Department in Washington, they were allowed to pass. Later, the Yunnan government purchased four more aircraft, which were obtained from a French trading house.

All goods passing through Indochina are subject to various taxes, with the exception of tin exports, which are exempt under treaty. The amount of each tax is proportional to the tax on goods consumed within Indochina. French goods imported into Indochina, of course, have lower tariff rates than foreign goods, and the same is true of transit taxes. Therefore, French goods have an advantage over non-French goods imported into Yunnan, and Chinese goods are similarly discriminated against. At present, the Yunnan government is negotiating with the French to give Chinese goods a slight advantage over non-French foreign goods, but when the reporter drafted this article, France had not yet approved the agreement. At present, the total amount of various transit taxes is at least 5% of the value of French goods and up to 15% of the value of non-French goods.

Various transit taxes and freight rates are frequently changed drastically without prior notice to foreign merchants. The purpose is to favor French merchants. For example, several years ago, an American merchant competed with French and British merchants to supply the Yunnan government with water pipes. The American merchant's bid was very low, and he was confident that he would not be defeated by the French merchant. However, the contract was eventually won by the French merchant. It was later learned that when the French water pipes arrived in Haiphong, Hanoi station posted a notice stating that the transit tax on water pipes had been temporarily reduced, and the railway freight rate had also been temporarily reduced by the railway bureau.

In addition to the above-mentioned monopolistic methods, there are frequent complaints about delays and damage in the transportation of non-French goods. It is said that French goods are transported from Haiphong to Yunnan very quickly, while non-French goods often take two to six months to arrive. As such, although French trade in other parts of China is far less than that of the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan, it is not surprising that it accounts for more than 60% of Yunnan's foreign trade.

Among foreign trade in Yunnan, the U.S. accounts for 20%, the U.K. accounts for 15%, and other non-French countries (mainly Germany and Japan) account for only 5%. As for foreign merchants, there is only one German, who is employed by a small Chinese hydroelectric company. There are no non-French foreign merchants in Yunnan Province. Besides French commerce, all the small amount of foreign commerce, such as the Standard Oil Company, etc., is operated by Chinese.

Although Yunnan is China's second-largest province, with an area of 146,714 square miles, it is not an important commercial area. It has a population of only 11 million, two-thirds of whom are Han Chinese and one-third of whom are Miao. The Miao people are mostly very poor. Foreign trade, excluding munitions, which are not included in customs reports, totaled US$20,556,194 in 1930 and fell to US$4,582,921 in 1932.

Tin and opium are Yunnan's two major exports. The former is mostly sold to the United States, and the latter is sold entirely within the country. The total value of tin production is about US$3.6 million per year, and opium is worth three times as much as tin.

About 2% of the province's arable land is dedicated to growing opium. Rice must be imported from outside. Agricultural land accounts for only a small portion of the province's area, so the people in some areas often suffer from famine. Opium is the main source of private profit for the military. Its taxes account for 20% of the province's public revenue. Opium smokers are prevalent throughout the province, more so than in any other province of China that I have visited.

In addition to tin, Yunnan also produces many other minerals, such as coal, lead, zinc, copper, antimony, silver, and large quantities of low-quality iron. Only tin mines are widely mined. The French have never demanded the development of various mines, at least for the time being, they are content with exclusively controlling railway transportation.

The main component of the Yunnan government is the military oligarchy, led by General Long Yun. It nominally obeys Nanjing, but in reality, it is completely independent. Long does not seem to be overly friendly with the French, but he has to associate with them in order to obtain military supplies. According to the Chinese side, the French maintain a firm control over Yunnan's finances. This statement is largely supported by authoritative neutral parties, as the price of silver dollars in Yunnan fluctuates from time to time due to the unstable financial situation of the province. When the government obtains loans in Shanghai or Hong Kong through the sale of tin or opium, these loans are often bought by French banks. The bank has a branch in the provincial capital, which is the only foreign bank in Yunnan Province.

French ambitions in other areas of southwest China are not obvious. Since 1914, there has been a plan to build a railway along the coast between Guangzhou Bay in Guangdong Province and the Indochina border, through Guangxi and Yunnan Provinces, and reaching Chongqing via Xufu in Sichuan Province. The contract for this railway was negotiated between the former Beijing government and the Sino-French Industrial Bank. The bank even advanced some funds to the Beijing government. Later, the bank went bankrupt, and the funds were not repaid. The draft contract did not stipulate that the contract would be voided if the conditions were not fulfilled. To date, France has neither transferred the contract to another French company nor canceled it. Therefore, in addition to controlling the Yunnan Railway, France holds this vested right in the entire southwest and has a special geographical interest.

As for other countries, apart from Japan and China, most have conflicting interests with France's policy. The United Kingdom regards Burma and Tibet as protectorates and is also watching Sichuan with interest. All three places are adjacent to Yunnan. The Soviet Union considers Tibet a buffer state between Russia and British India and, of course, cannot ignore the future of Tibet. Therefore, France's Far Eastern empire and its imperialistic ambitions are deeply related to the balance of power in Asia.

Huang Fu Passes Through Hankou to Jiangxi 95

Visiting Chiang to Seek Instructions on North China Diplomacy

Tang Youren Travels East on the Dehe Steamer

Hankou Correspondence: Huang Fu, Chairman of the Beiping Political Affairs Committee, traveled south from Beiping on the 3rd to seek instructions from Chairman Chiang and President Wang on the diplomatic situation in North China, which is tense. Accompanying him were Secretary He Jiecai, Wang Dagang, Councilor Ge Chongxun, Gao Shiluan, and several attendants, as well as a platoon of soldiers from the 105th Division as escorts. He arrived in Hankou at 10:30 AM on the 5th. After Huang got off the train, he went to the Central Bank Building for a short rest. Zhang Xueliang and others crossed the river to visit him, exchanging views on the military and political situation in North China and consulting on some matters. That night at 8:00 PM, Huang took the Dehe steamer to Jiangxi. Tang Youren also traveled with him. Huang made a statement in Hankou, saying, "Due to various diplomatic and political matters in North China, I need to report to the Central Government, Chairman Chiang, and President Wang, and seek instructions on future policies. I took the train from Beiping to Hankou on the afternoon of the 3rd, and took the opportunity to visit Vice Commander Zhang to catch up. After visiting Chairman Chiang in Jiangxi, I will stay for about four days, then go to Nanjing to visit President Wang, stay in Nanjing for a week, and then return to Hangzhou via Shanghai to sweep the tombs. The estimated return trip will take about 40 days. In recent years, the administration and diplomacy in North China have been handled in accordance with the Central Government's consistent policies, and I still maintain this intention. Important passes on the Great Wall, such as Yuguan, have already been completely taken over. Currently, only passes such as Malanyu are still awaiting recovery. We will continue to negotiate. The issue of opening traffic and mail was raised and discussed several times by the Japanese side at the beginning of the Eastward takeover, but it was suspended due to disagreements. In the future, if we consult with the Japanese side on this matter, we will proceed on the principle of never violating the Central Government's principle of not recognizing the puppet organization and not splitting the four eastern provinces. The Japanese have recruited thousands of Chinese laborers to serve in the military. Because there is no clear identification, it is difficult to distinguish them. I have ordered them to be strictly guarded against. As for their reinforcement of troops in Chahar East, the fact is very obvious. Inner Mongolian autonomy may be affected by this. However, the Bailingmiao Autonomous Political Affairs Committee is scheduled to be established at the end of this month, which is certainly sufficient to deal with the situation. The Tangshan labor unrest is currently being mediated and should come to an end within days and will not be expanded or prolonged. The unrest of plainclothes teams in Qingdao City is mostly composed of local hooligans. Perhaps there is some instigation from a certain party, but it is not known. The remnants of Sun Dianying's troops have been urged by the Jin-Sui army to reorganize, and they have complied. There should be no further disputes in the future. The Yutian Security Team is also being reorganized and should be completed in the short term. The security of North China is very consolidated, and everything can be reorganized step by step. The rumors that the Political Affairs Committee will expand its organization are absolutely untrue, and there is no need for it. After I leave Beiping, the affairs of the Political Affairs Committee will be handled by Secretary-General He Qigong on my behalf." Tang Youren also said, "This time I came to Hankou on the orders of President Wang to urge Shi Ying to return to Beijing to resume his duties. I visited Mayor Shi the day before yesterday and conveyed President Wang's sincere condolences and requests to stay. Mayor Shi has agreed to return to Beijing, but he needs to postpone it for a few days to take care of private affairs. I am busy with official duties, so I am returning east first. The situation in North China is not only diplomatically serious, but other situations are also very complicated. I have not yet fully understood the recent situation of the Ban Hong incident because I was on official business outside. At this time, when the borders are troubled and the crisis is urgent, only by improving internal affairs can we use diplomacy. I hope that everyone will work together to save the situation." It is heard that Huang Fu's trip south is indeed of important task, and it is rumored that Japanese Ambassador Ariyoshi has postponed his return home to meet with Huang in Beijing. However, Huang made no comment on this in Hankou. (5th)

Bandit Liu Occupies Ganyu, JiangSu 96

｜Wang Jun's Troops Strictly Guard Against the Escape of Remnant Bandits｜

Xuzhou Correspondence: After the remnant bandits of Liu Guitang occupied Ganyu County, Wang Jun, in addition to ordering Li Shilong's brigade, which was stationed on the eastern road, to suppress them, also went east by special train to Xin'an Town yesterday (the 4th) at noon to supervise the suppression. According to the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Security Department, when the Liu bandits attacked Ganyu County on the 3rd, the Ganyu police force was weak. Upon hearing the news of the bandits' arrival, they were unable to hold on and withdrew outside the city, allowing the bandits to enter the city unopposed. However, behind the bandits, there was a Shandong army regiment that also pursued them into Ganyu. The bandits stayed in the county seat for one night and fled south on the morning of the 4th. At this time, the 7th Division troops sent by Wang Jun had already advanced north from Caopu and Baitabu stations to intercept the bandits. The bandits were impatient to fight and fled as soon as they were attacked. They turned back and fled north, and are now in Huandun, at the junction of Jiangsu and Shandong. The 7th Division troops are searching and suppressing Huandun from Shahe Shangdun. The Shandong army, which pursued the bandits towards Ganyu, is also converging on Huandun. They will be able to reach Huandun today to besiege them. Wang Jun has advanced from Xin'an Town to Niushan Station to command the suppression. Trenches have been dug and defensive fortifications have been built in Xinpu and Haizhou to prevent the bandits from escaping. As for the situation in Ganyu, it is heard that the bandits looted a lot of property in the city, and some of the police's weapons were confiscated. It is rumored that the county magistrate escaped when the bandits entered the city and has now returned to the county to deal with the aftermath. However, the details of the losses have not yet been confirmed. The eastern section of the Longhai Railway is operating as usual. After the 19th Brigade advanced north to pursue the bandits, the newly transferred 21st Brigade on the eastern road is heavily guarded along the line. Wang plans to telegraph Chiang Kai-shek if necessary to increase the number of troops to encircle and suppress the bandits, in order to completely eliminate them, and plans to request the dispatch of aircraft for reconnaissance and bombing. (5th)

Autonomy is Promoted in Fujian Province 97

The Department of Civil Affairs Orders All Counties to Handle Matters Within a Time Limit

Fuzhou Correspondence: Li Zuyu, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, went to Jiangxi at the beginning of last month to attend the administrative meeting and handed over the affairs of the department to the chief secretary, Li Mo, to act as his agent. Now Li Zuyu has returned to Fujian from Jiangxi on the 3rd of this month. The next day, he attended the Provincial Government Committee meeting to report on the trip to Jiangxi. Regarding the future civil administration plan of this province, it is heard that special emphasis will be placed on promoting autonomy and dealing with the aftermath in the bandit areas. The autonomy of various counties in Fujian Province was ordered to be suspended by the puppet government, and many have not yet been restored. Now, the first phase of the local autonomy to be handled in various counties has been formulated, including four items: investigating the population, organizing neighborhoods, electing officials, and completing the Baojia system. They are limited to being completed within six months. In the second phase, major policies such as sanitation, education, afforestation, and road construction will be implemented. Once they are submitted to the Provincial Government Committee for approval, they can be ordered to be implemented in various counties.

Regarding the problem of dealing with the aftermath in the bandit areas, the Department of Civil Affairs has urged the various county magistrates to go to their posts with the army as soon as possible to preside over local administration. Administrative commissioners will be set up in the northern and western Fujian areas to supervise the county magistrates in handling the aftermath. The proposal to set up commissioners will also be submitted to the Provincial Committee Meeting and submitted to the Nanchang Headquarters for approval after it is passed. It can be implemented roughly next month. To relieve the people in the bandit areas, the first step is to revive the rural areas. The measures are all in accordance with those promulgated by the Nanchang Headquarters, which are (1) clearing land, (2) lending funds, (3) exempting old rents. (4th)

Huainan, Xiang, Hubei, West Anhui Four Shores Transportation Merchants Appeal 98

Forcefully Argue the Key to Salt Transportation Interests

Hoping the Government Will Pay Attention to Relief

Huainan, Xiang, Hubei, West Anhui four shores transportation merchants, on the 3rd, sent an express mail telegram, the text reads: [Central Party Headquarters, National Government, Military Commission, Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Judicial Yuan, Control Yuan, Examination Yuan, Chairman Lin, Chairman Chiang, Heads of various Yuan, various Commissioners, various Ministers, Provincial Government Chairman, Provincial Government Commissioners, all responsible superiors, all National Federation of Commerce, all public legal entities, all newspapers, respectfully, we merchants have gathered capital to operate salt transportation, spending tens of thousands in costs, enduring thousands of miles of wind and wave danger, accumulating stock for more than a year, to profit by mere pennies, enriching the national tax revenue above, and aiding people's food supply below. On one hand, we abide by the restrictions of laws and regulations, and on the other hand, we rely on the protection of laws and regulations. We uphold the law and serve the public, without exceeding this. Last year, the long-standing practice of allowing tax exemptions and transportation subsidies for salt loss was stopped. Merchants, fearful of the impermanence of natural disasters and man-made calamities, ran around appealing for rescue, waiting for months without a reply. This year, the new scale was adopted, with unclear distinctions between tare weight and salt weight. Shopkeepers took the opportunity to attack and withhold merchant capital. The audit offices on each shore even ordered competitive sales, advance tax payment, and price reductions. We have presented the difficulties and circumstances to the responsible superiors at all levels, but have not received solutions. The merchants' situation is urgent and difficult to advance or retreat. We dare to present the difficult points separately.

Xiang, Hubei, West Anhui do not produce salt. It is transported from afar, passing through the Yangtze River and large lakes to inland rivers, and then distributed to each shore. The circumstances are different from land transportation and short-distance resale in other provinces, or on-site collection. Although transportation subsidies are requested, the fact that for one dan of salt, half a dan of field tax is paid, and the price and freight of two dan of salt are used, is clearly evident in the hardship and fatigue. If the facts are doubted and everything is overturned due to the inability to conduct immediate investigation and inspection, then it is like refusing to eat for fear of choking, how can fairness and reason be obtained? Moreover, although salt is transported by merchants, it is actually sold by the government. The shore tax is collected from the shopkeepers who buy salt, not from the transportation merchants. If the salt is lost, where will the tax come from? Ships encountering danger is a common occurrence worldwide. Suffering losses from danger is already painful. If one is further required to compensate for the tax on goods not received by the person who bought the goods, no such system exists in any country in the world. Some say that insuring sail-transported salt is possible. However, cargo insurance only covers merchant capital. If field and shore taxes exceed the merchant capital by two or three times, which is unheard of for other goods, the insurance premium would be enormous, where would the funds come from? Moreover, on the Xiang shore, the inland river transfer, side shores, and rocky beaches are constantly dangerous, and the amount of salt stored and the weight of shore tax are unparalleled in other provinces. Between spring and summer, mountain floods break out, and the salt stored in warehouses is a constant concern. Companies are unwilling to insure it, and the situation is indeed difficult. If merchants are required to compensate for losses, then distributing to each shore will inevitably be difficult. The impact on the people's food supply and tax revenue will be enormous. It is requested that tax exemptions and transportation subsidies should still be granted for the amount of salt actually lost, which cannot be salvaged by human power.

As for the middle and west road side shores of the Xiang shore, dangerous shoals stand, and waterfalls are steep. Some are hundreds of miles away, others are thousands of miles away. Ships travel in the midst of chaotic stone peaks, pulled up purely by human power. Each ticket is divided into dozens of ships, and danger occurs in more than one ship or place. Therefore, it was previously stipulated that each ticket would be allowed a tax exemption and transportation subsidy for twenty loads, to show a limit. Even if there is more loss, the merchant pays the tax, which is actually due to the terrain and is not desired by the merchant. If the practice of allowing exemption for loss is abolished, it is requested that some funds be allocated from the fees collected from the belly shore for attaching to the side, along with the merchant capital, to provide subsidies. This is one.

Xiang, Hubei, and West three shores have always released salt using the Sima scale. Each load of tax salt is 100 catties, tare weight 5 catties, brine loss 4 catties. Upon arrival at the shore for sale, the local customary scale is used to weigh it out of the warehouse. The Sima scale is 100 catties, equivalent to more than 102 or 3 catties on the customary scale. The weight system is 16 taels and 8 mace per catty. According to Article 5 of the tax regulations, for tax measurement, each catty is allowed to add 8 mace of salt loss in addition to the legally defined 16 taels. This salt loss is to compensate the transportation merchant for the transportation responsibility. Merchants buy 100 catties of salt in the warehouse, which is equivalent to more than 107 catties on the local 16-tael scale. The 5 catties of tare weight is the salt loss that the transportation merchants should receive, which is transferred and issued to the merchants along with the scale. The 5 catties of tare weight outside the scale is moved into the remaining catties of the 320-load tax package, using the field tax to subsidize the merchants and collect the shore tax. However, Anhui shore has always clearly removed the tare weight, so each ticket pays 28 loads in excess. This year, the new scale is adopted, using the Sima scale 100 catties, converted to 127 catties on the market scale. The original scale surplus and the 8 mace of salt loss used to offset the tare weight are all included in the regular catties for taxation. Hengshan merchants in Hunan said that the transportation merchants were using tare as salt, and attacked with telegrams, withholding merchant capital. Now the entire province's weight system is limited to a unified time. Merchants buy and sell salt catties, using the same market scale for entry and exit. For the price of 100 catties, they get 94 catties of salt. It is feared that the public will also raise objections. It is requested that the weight of tare be clearly removed for each load to prevent disputes. The Sima scale 5 catties of tare weight must be removed and given to the merchants, and the 8 mace of salt loss per catty and the scale surplus converted from the original Sima scale customary scale are all incorporated into the regular load, collecting field and shore taxes. The surplus salt from the previous 320 loads of shore tax payment is now eliminated due to consolidation, and there are no more surplus catties to speak of. However, the 8 mace of merchant capital was originally collected at 1,600 taels per 100 catties. Now it is reduced based on 1,680 taels, which has disappeared in effect. Moreover, the field tax within the 320 loads that subsidizes the merchants is again moved into 5 loads for collection. Since the facts have changed, the merchant capital should be determined. This is two.

Merchants transport salt and often prepare for more than half a year, up to eighteen or nineteen months, because sales have a fixed time and price, which can be estimated in advance. Even if there is a loss, it is limited. The Hubei shore abolished the method of full-round guaranteed price and reduced prices for competitive sales. In one year, merchants lost more than a hundred thousand. Now the Xiang audit office is ordering it to be implemented in Xiang. Merchants in Xiang, seeing the situation in Hubei, are panicked as if a great disaster is about to occur. It is believed that the merchant capital on the four shores, since the regulations of the second year of the Republic of China, has been more than three yuan per 100 catties for more than twenty years. Compared with the increase in livelihood over the past twenty years and the need for transportation costs, it is impossible to reduce the price again. Only because there is too much salt in stock, speculators use this to estimate the sales of other merchants, and those who come later push forward, and those who come earlier suppress those who come later, taking away the interest on other merchants' stocks, under the name of price reductions, without reducing their inherent merchant capital. Merchants who should be sold in rounds have been storing in warehouses for a long time, and the interest on the stock is heavy. Suddenly, those who come later reduce prices and occupy their sales, and the longer they are suppressed, the more losses they incur. As a result, they will inevitably follow the price reduction, and because of the competitive sales, they have to be held hostage by the shopkeepers. In addition to the price reduction, they are followed by long-term credit. Once the credit is abused, bad debts increase. The Hubei shore has become a lesson, how can it be repeated on the Xiang, West, and Anhui shores, and make them follow in their footsteps, open the door to competition, open the road to speculation, eliminate established methods, and merchants lose protection. Who will transport and store tens of thousands of merchant capital in shore warehouses for more than ten months, causing endless trouble? Powerful people compete in speculation, transport only after sales are completed, and the warehouse has no storage for a month. The people suffer from light food, and the field and shore tax revenue is increasingly insufficient. If there is an emergency, there is no borrowing. What is the benefit of official and merchant difficulties? If it is said that this can promote sales, it is also felt that it is not. Salt is food, a little is not allowed, and more is not possible. The hinterland originally belongs to Huai sales, without the encroachment of neighboring private sales. The people do not eat more because of the cheap price, and the sales will not increase as a result. If the remote areas are flooded with smuggled salt, the reduction of several cents of merchant capital cannot compete. The government's expenses have regular monthly payments. If advance tax payment is used to stimulate a temporary increase, borrowing from the future, how will it be sustained in the future? The regular way of tax administration should not be like this. It is requested to withdraw the order for competitive sales, advance tax payment, and price reduction, and still order the method of guaranteed list price for sales in order, to stabilize commerce. This is three.

The above points are all important keys to salt transportation. Now, fortunately, salt affairs officials from various provinces are meeting in the capital to discuss the gains and losses of salt administration. Merchants have sent representatives to Beijing to petition, and dare to present the advantages and disadvantages in detail to the intelligent ears. It is hoped that you will grant a review, preside over political justice, to maintain salt transportation and protect tax revenue, and cannot bear the urgency of awaiting orders. Huainan, Xiang, Hubei, West Anhui four shores transportation merchants kowtow. ]

Page 10

Anhui Chamber of Commerce Again Requests Verification and Reduction of Salt Tax 99

Wuhu correspondence, after the Ministry of Finance implemented the new scale for salt catties, merchants in Anhui province have repeatedly appealed to allow the salt price to be reduced according to the shortage of catties in the new scale, but have not been approved. The Provincial Chamber of Commerce, because the local chambers of commerce are still requesting, yesterday submitted a detailed statement to the Ministry of Finance, detailing the advantages and disadvantages, and requesting verification and reduction to relieve the people's difficulties. The original text is as follows: [This chamber of commerce sent a telegram on January 12 of this year, requesting that the Ministry convert the salt catties to the new market scale and reduce the salt price. The Ministry replied in telegram 30, stating that the telegram was received, and the matter had been reported by the Wuhu Chamber of Commerce and others. It was stated that the conversion to the new scale was a uniform procedure in various provinces, and the request to reduce the new market scale salt price according to the Sima scale salt price should not be discussed. It was replied in the case that matters concerning laws and regulations should be properly persuaded and diligently followed. It was intended to entrust the relevant responsibilities to the affiliated chambers of commerce in Anhui province, and to give guidance in accordance with telegram 30. Now, the various chambers of commerce have stated that the conversion of salt catties to the new market scale is an expression of implementing the new system of weights and measures. Therefore, the Ministry's advisory document No. 202 states that the salt affairs and tax affairs agencies under the Ministry have always used only measuring instruments for the assessment of goods, which is easier to prepare and should be converted as soon as possible to promote it. It can be seen that the conversion to the new scale is not for the purpose of increasing taxes, but now the reform of the weight system has become a hidden increase in the tax rate, which is incomprehensible. Salt is a necessary food for the entire population, and the increase in salt prices makes the poor suffer even more. Therefore, in the middle of the Qing Dynasty, the minister requested to increase the price by three or four coins per catty, and the upright frontier minister insisted that it was not possible. Now, with the conversion to the new market scale, the price is increased by more than sixty or seventy coins per catty, without the approval of the Legislative Yuan, increasing the suffering of the poor. Even if it becomes a law, this is incomprehensible. The implementation of the new system should be based on laws and regulations. Now, according to the weight system recorded in the Weights and Measures Law, one is the standard system and the other is the market system. Article 11 stipulates that the market system is only allowed to be temporarily used between private buying and selling transactions. As for the government tax collection agencies, they should of course implement the standard system. However, why can the customs adopt the standard system kilogram scale, and the salt affairs audit office use the market scale for releasing scales and collecting taxes, which is only temporarily used in private buying and selling transactions? It has gone beyond the law, but it is still said that it concerns laws and regulations, which is incomprehensible. For the sake of rectifying salt affairs and averaging the burden, the tax rate of 20 yuan or more has been reduced to 10 yuan, and those with 10 yuan or more will be gradually improved. However, after the six counties in Huizhou implemented the new market scale, each load was clearly reduced by 6 cents and 7.6 mils and secretly increased by 1 yuan and 1 cent and 9.6 mils. Before long, they ordered each load to increase the price by 4 cents and 6 mils. Only increases are seen, and no reductions are heard. Is it that the tax rates in the past were all below the legal limit, so it is necessary to add both openly and secretly to average the burden? This is incomprehensible. In short, since the revolution, additional taxes have been added to salt catties on the Anhui shore. For example, the temporary additional tax in the 16th year of the Republic of China was two yuan per stone, the additional Northern Expedition fee in the 17th year of the Republic of China was one yuan and five cents per load, the construction fee in the 18th year of the Republic of China was one dime per load, and the listed price in the 20th year of the Republic of China was three dimes per load. Most of them are temporary in nature and should be abolished uniformly when rectifying salt administration, and the people should start anew. Moreover, in this autumn of rural bankruptcy and economic depression, how can we increase the burden on merchants and the people? Your chamber is responsible for maintaining the market and requesting the government to maintain responsibility. Please do not avoid axes and cutwords, and immediately present the matter. Please reduce the salt price according to the shortage of salt catties to benefit the whole people, etc. It is found that the people in various places only know that the salt tax has been clearly ordered to be reduced, but they cannot clearly understand the content of secretly increasing the salt price by changing the scale. Therefore, when buying salt from sub-stores, disputes often arise due to increased value, and there is even a fear of not being able to sell salt in many places. It is necessary to provide relief to avoid affecting the whole people. This chamber of commerce has already received earnest requests from local merchants and the people, and has to risk petitioning the Ministry to consider that the additional burden on the Anhui shore is already heavy, and to allow the salt price to be reduced according to the shortage of catties in the new scale to benefit the poor and stabilize commerce. We cannot bear the urgency of awaiting orders. ] (3rd)

Cotton Control Association Investigates Cotton Weaving

Songyi is a cotton-producing area. Historically, cotton fabrics manufactured in Song include yarn blankets, cotton socks, and towels. Yarn blankets and socks are particularly popular. However, due to years of turmoil and social and economic panic, sales have plummeted. Small-scale factories have closed down one after another, and manufacturers with some capital have also suffered heavy losses due to accumulated inventory and poor sales, affecting people's livelihoods. Recently, the Cotton Industry Control Group of the National Economic Commission sent a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce, stating that it will send personnel to Song to investigate cotton textiles and requesting assistance and facilitation. Today, the association sent Wang Bohua and Mr. Ma to Song to state the investigation mission, saying that they intend to improve various cotton textiles with American cotton. The current investigation includes the categories, costs, and sales of cotton textiles, and what taxes and levies are levied along the way, to provide a basis for improvement and to develop the revival of industry to save and strengthen our country.

Qinfeng Yarn Factory Labor Strike Expands 100

The female workers in the weaving and spinning departments of the Qinfeng Textile Factory's first workshop in Zhoushanbang, this county, went on strike due to the factory's excessive fines. Both labor and management have petitioned the party and government agencies for relief. For the sake of public order, the county government, in addition to sending Zhang Yu, the chief inspector of the Public Security Bureau, to investigate, also ordered the county police team to maintain order at the factory. At about 4:00 p.m. on the 5th, the night shift female workers of the factory happened to be going to work, and the police closed the alley gates, refusing them to go to work. The female workers were furious and uttered obscenities, saying, [You are all capitalist running dogs]. Then some people threw stones at the police officers, and another group of female workers, holding chamber pots, clashed with the police officers. For a time, the order was chaotic. The other four people, Yu Rendi, Liu Yuxian, Chen Sanmei, and Bao Afeng, were also beaten with gun butts, and their heads were bleeding. The situation was pitiful. There was also a male worker, Xu Ajin, who was also injured. The storm led to expansion. That night, the injured female workers were carried to the county government, requesting an injury verification and requesting that the perpetrators be arrested and brought to justice. They were stopped by the gatekeepers, who told them to handle it tomorrow. Yesterday (6th), all the workers of the factory went on strike, and a female worker, Bao Afeng, was placed under the supervision of the county government. At 9:00 a.m., all the workers held a discussion meeting at the Dunrenli Textile Industry Union, and decided to go to the county government to petition, demanding the release of the arrested female worker Bao Afeng. The matter was learned by the county party headquarters, and it telegraphed the association to suspend the proceedings. At 1:00 p.m., the association invited Ye Qin Ding Heling, Shenxin Pan Quanbao, Li Guisheng, Guangqin Zhao Xiongfei, Chen Can Gen, Yukang Hu Tiankai, Wang Genbao, and more than a dozen others to hold an emergency joint meeting of various factory textile factories, deciding that the offices of each factory should provide assistance in unison, proceeding in three steps: the first step is to publish a notice in the newspaper to inform the factories to provide assistance, and the second and third steps will be discussed at a meeting depending on the development of the situation to discuss coping strategies. Currently, the workers have agreed to resume work after being persuaded by both the party and the government, but the factory is firm and unwilling to start work, and must stop for a week or two weeks, and stated that when necessary, they will use hard-line measures to replace all the workers. In order to solve the labor strike, the county party headquarters also held a meeting at 2:00 p.m. yesterday with Ye Dezhen, secretary of the county government, and Yao Fusheng, a clerk, to discuss mediation principles.

Bizarre Murder Case Occurs in Xizhai 101

Lu A'mei, a hired worker of Zou Jiazhen, a resident of Xizhai in the second district, was 37 years old and unmarried. He worked diligently on weekdays. Zou Juntai, a clansman of the Zou family, is a local rich man and is currently the head of the security corps. There are many servants in the house, including a male servant named A'jia, who is in his twenties. He and A'mei were close friends, but A'jia was fond of gambling. In January of this year, he lost a lot of money, so he took the opportunity to steal the host's crepe quilt and pawned it to A'mei for one yuan. In the middle of this month, A'mei was drying the quilt on the field, but it was spotted by Zhang Ganyun, the wife of Juntai. Zhang asked A'mei, who said that A'jia had pawned it to me. Zhang went home and planned to question A'jia, but A'jia had disappeared. Zhang then accused A'mei of colluding in theft and informed Juntai of the situation. Juntai then led a group of corps members to privately torture A'mei to force a confession. Later, the villagers became suspicious because A'mei suddenly disappeared. It was not until about 11:00 a.m. on the 4th of this month that the body was suddenly found in the rice bin of Zou Juntai's house. The body was contorted, the head was swollen, and there was a white waist band around the neck. Zou Shiling, the head of the map in the area, reported to the county prosecutor's office on the previous day, requesting an autopsy. Yesterday (6th) afternoon, Prosecutor Shen led officials to the countryside for an autopsy.

Security Office Executes Red Pill Trafficker 108

(Special Feature) The Terror of Yellow Trade Translated by Yang Deheng 109

Original article published in Tbe Neue Weltbubqe, Praga LiberalWeekly, German,

Summarized and translated by Max Rudert in Readers Dizest,

Japan's terror to world trade can be seen in the following price list. The one who holds the reins in the world market must of course be able to sell cheaper than his competitors. And the selling price of Japan in the European market can be roughly distinguished, with the following numbers:

X X

Electric light bulbs at two and a half cents each, in gold dollars

Men's socks at four and a half cents each

Gold nib fountain pens at seven and a half cents each

Nine-piece coffee set at forty-nine cents per set

Bicycles at four dollars and fifty-six cents each

Her cotton fabrics can be 40% to 70% lower in cost than European factory products. For example, the selling price of Japan's best rayon in Marseille is lower than the yarn price in Lyon. One can imagine that a European industrialist once said, "Even if my raw materials were stolen and my labor costs unpaid, I'm afraid I still couldn't compete with this price."

This astonishingly low selling price is also due to their long working hours, low wages, and the systematic 60% inflation of the Japanese yen. The remuneration for workers working ten to twelve hours a day is as follows:

Coal miners, 26 cents

Silk weaving workers, 35 cents

Mechanics, 81 cents

Potters, 53 cents

Match workers, 33 cents

In addition, child labor over the age of ten, which is allowed in Japan, also occupies a considerable position in the domestic labor force, working ten to twelve hours a day for only four cents.

Forced labor, endurance of hunger, and simple living, like the children of the aforementioned child labor, coupled with modern production tools, the power of this youngest capitalist is expanding in the world, comparatively making the economic means of the Chinese unable to come to the fore. From 1932 to 1933, she had nine large-scale new factories producing rayon. Other industries also progressed unbelievably, all benefiting from the highest gains of modern industry. The following is her average analysis of various industries from 1932 to 1933 - years of recession in various countries around the world:

Industrial Classification Percentage

Cement and paper 12.9

Steel 13.5

Machinery 15.1

Yarn factories 18.2

Woolen fabrics 23.1

Rayon 24.9

This analysis is not inferred from her domestic market. The weakness of her people's purchasing power had to force her to take the path of challenging dumping. In her "Ten-Year Export Plan", subsidized by the government, she is preparing to deal with the world market. Indeed, it is now developing brilliantly. Export agencies have established associations to study the needs of foreign markets and the tariffs of various countries. Sales departments have been established in key areas, causing the whole world to be hit by her shockingly low prices. Recently, in British-controlled territories such as Australia, New Zealand, the Straits Settlements, India, etc., there have already been alarming effects. Although Britain is doing its best to oppose the Japanese trade invasion, she is still resolutely proceeding. The import of Indian cotton fabrics has increased fivefold, and yarn has increased fourfold.

The same is true in Africa. From Cape Town in the far south, Japanese salesmen can be found everywhere, all the way to the Congo and Abyssinia. In the first seven months of 1933, of the 870,000 yards of rayon imported into Tanganyika, 800,000 yards were exported from Japan. As for the Near East, especially Iraq, Persia, and Egypt, Japan has successful markets.

The British market has suffered the most damage and is struggling to survive under this full-scale dumping. Raising tariffs has only resisted her weakest points. If she further increases her protective tariffs, then when London increases its demands to curb Japanese low-priced goods, Japan will issue a warning note to Britain, saying that it will no longer buy cotton from India or Australia, but will procure it from South America. However, since the wool industry in Australia and the cotton industry in India have been in recession due to changes in their economic status, Japanese goods are voluntarily promoted in the British market regardless of price.

Japan's operations are almost as alarming everywhere. According to the statistics of foreign trade recently released by Tokyo in 1932, one can see:

Market Percentage Increase

Asia 59.3

Europe 29.3

North America 28.5

Central America 41.3

South America 21.8

Africa 96.2

Australia 76.9

This represents an average increase of 51 percent. At the same time, the world's commerce has also suffered this loss.

Japan is organizing a Central European Trade Bureau in Vienna, so her power will invade the markets of the Balkan Peninsula, Central Europe, and Southern Europe. A large-scale warehouse is being built, preparing to store large quantities of cotton, wool, silk, rayon, steel, rubber, celluloid, porcelain, paper goods, as well as light bulbs, auto parts, bicycles, and other goods. From then on, there will be one more promotion center. The increase in protective tariffs, which is most feared by other countries, does not hinder the old goods. Barren countries have conditions for exchanging goods with Japan. Japan is a country that does not export agricultural products, which can give it a lot more benefits than other industrialized countries.

But to come back to the point, the final systematic results of Japan cannot take her initial success as a standard. Japanese imperialists lack coal and minerals. This lack makes her finally weak, just like her excessive exports. Germany and Britain never export a quarter of their total production, and the United States exports no more than 10 to 12 percent, while Japan has reached 60 percent. This large-scale invasion of the world trade market contains the seeds of its own destruction. Her foundation may be shattered in this situation. The outward appearance of alarm is only a manifestation of the most rabid achievements of her people. In political and military terms, Japan also has various difficulties and terrors. The relationship with the United States and the Soviet Union has also reached a serious symbolic point.

Japan is like a cauldron, and its pressure is constantly rising. Within ten years, her population has increased from 56,000,000 to 66,000,000. With the help of the government, a large industrial base has been established, and manic exports are also progressing. Will Japan stop - or will it inevitably - before social disintegration occurs on her overpopulated island? Her current military aggression against Manchuria, the annual military defense spending of 1,200,000,000 yuan, and the tendency towards frenzied Fascism are not expressions of her rising image? An old Japanese proverb also says, "It is difficult to get off the back of a tiger."

Articles of the Italian Boxer Indemnity Loan Silver Group 6% Securities 111

Decision to Issue on the 15th

According to Guo Wen News Agency, the Italian Boxer Indemnity Loan Silver Group 6% securities is now scheduled to be issued on the 15th of this month. Now, the text of the articles has been found and transcribed as follows:

Article 1 of the Articles of the Italian Boxer Indemnity Loan Silver Group 6% Securities of the Republic of China, Year 23: This silver group, based on Article 11 of the contract signed with the Ministry of Finance on January 27, Republic of China, Year 23, for the Italian refund of the Boxer Indemnity to offset the national currency of 44 million yuan, will issue securities of 30 million yuan in one lump sum, named the Italian Boxer Indemnity Loan Silver Group 6% Securities. Article 2: This security is scheduled to be issued on April 15, Republic of China, Year 23. Article 3: The interest rate of this security is set at 6% per week, and interest is paid every six months. Article 4: This security will be repaid once every six months, determined by lottery. Article 5: This security will be repaid in full in twelve installments over six years from the date of issuance, in accordance with the principal and interest repayment schedule of this silver group. Article 6: The Central, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications are designated as the repayment agencies for the repayment of principal and interest of this security. Article 7: In addition to the principal and interest fund allocated by the Ministry of Finance under the Italian Boxer Indemnity Loan contract designated by this silver group as the fund for the payment of principal and interest of this security, this silver group is fully responsible for the repayment. Article 8: This security is issued at full face value. Article 9: The denominations of this security are 10,000 yuan and 1,000 yuan. Article 10: This security is designated as unregistered. Article 11: This security may be recalled by this silver group upon three months' notice. If the market price of the security is higher than the face value on the date of the notice, it will be recalled according to the market price on the date of the notice. If the market price is lower than the face value, it will be recalled at face value. All interest will be calculated daily from the date of the notice according to the face value until the date of recall. Article 12: This security may be freely traded and mortgaged. Article 13: Anyone who forges this security or damages its credit will be punished according to law. Article 14: The articles of this security will be submitted by this silver group to the Ministry of Finance for filing and implementation.

Investigation of Imported Foreign Sugar 115

Annual Amount Reaches 14 Million Piculs, Worth 100 Million Yuan

The Ministry of Industry Plans to Persuade Overseas Chinese to Invest in Restoring Domestic Sugar

China's sugar industry used to be very developed. Later, due to the cession of Taiwan and the impact of the recession, the output gradually declined. In addition, foreign sugar took the opportunity to import and arbitrarily lowered prices to dump, causing China's sugar industry to be on the verge of collapse. According to investigations by the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and the customs, the largest import volume of foreign sugar each year reaches 14 million piculs, worth more than 100 million yuan, ranking second among foreign imports. In order to restore the domestic sugar industry and recover rights and interests, Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo plans to consult with overseas Chinese tycoons on investment methods during his upcoming visit to the Nanyang Islands, so as to first restore the sugar industry in Min, Yue, Qiongya, Chaozhang, and the Sichuan River, and then set up large-scale sugar factories to restore and recover rights and interests.

Danger to Chinese Copper Skin Factories Under Japanese Dumping 122

Request for Government to Devise Relief Measures

The copper skin raw materials needed by China's hardware industry have always relied on imports, especially from Japan. Since Chinese people in Shanghai established the Zhonghua, Nanchang, Shanghai, Qixing, Huaxing, and Zhongguo copper skin factories, they have recovered considerable interests. Because the quality of domestic products is excellent and the prices are low, factories such as flashlight, thermos bottle, lock, and hardware factories are happy to use them. The manufactured goods are also more durable than foreign goods. Therefore, in the midst of this national product's vigorous development, foreign goods will gradually disappear. Unexpectedly, the Japanese are unwilling to give up their original position and adopt a dumping policy, selling at all costs to compete with Chinese merchants. Unscrupulous merchants are also taking advantage of this, importing large quantities privately, causing the business of various Chinese factories to plummet. In the near future, it is feared that all factories that need copper skin will be invaded by Japanese goods. In such a situation, how can the future not be dangerous? It is now heard that Mr. Yu Zhongnan, manager of the Zhonghua Copper Factory, seeing this crisis, has initiated a joint effort with all the copper factories in Shanghai to submit a petition to the government requesting relief measures. Yesterday, letters were sent to various copper factories to solicit opinions in order to proceed. The original letter is recorded below. We respectfully inform you that since the Japanese bandits occupied the Northeast, all Chinese people have been indignant. Everyone agrees that fundamental resistance is necessary to save us from danger. Fortunately, in the past two years, all businesses have been able to work hard to survive, and some progress has been made. The copper skin business, which has been monopolized by Japanese merchants for many years, has also seen a glimmer of hope. Unexpectedly, Japanese merchants have recently taken advantage of the decline in our market conditions and are unwilling to give up their original position, selling cheaply at a loss. The merchants who need copper skin are again greedy for profit and forget their hatred, and continue to import privately. Our copper industry has suffered a huge blow, and the impact is very profound. If we do not urgently seek remedies, the future crisis will be even more unimaginable. I deeply feel the pain and am concerned about my fellow countrymen. I plan to jointly petition the government for relief with various copper factories. You are a senior in the business world and have great patriotic enthusiasm. You must have many insightful views on this matter. If you agree, please give us your opinion so that we can schedule a meeting to discuss a good plan.

Resolved to formulate a detailed plan and notify separately. (8) Some of China's products, such as carpets, are often unable to participate in the exhibition due to limited resources. How should the association provide assistance? Resolved to subsidize the cost of shipping to the United States for display from the association's funds. (9) Additional economic members of the association are proposed. Resolved to add Zhang Xianglin as an economic member. Considering other countries, there are permanent central organizations that can cope with ease. Petition to the Ministry of Industry

Petition for a matter. Petition for a matter. It is learned that the member Zhong Xuezhun of the Hezhong Machinery Factory stated in a letter that the existence of factories in the concessions is sufficient to revitalize the market, and the Municipal Council should welcome it. Why is it suppressing it instead? The land price in the concessions is very expensive. Why are Chinese factories not located in the Chinese area but in the concessions? The reason is nothing more than that water, electricity, transportation, and protection are not yet properly arranged. (1) Water and electricity are both in Shanghai, separated by a boundary line, and the prices are different. The electricity meters are also inaccurate. The salaries of important employees of the water and electricity companies in the concessions are around 1,000 yuan, while the salaries of employees of the water and electricity companies in the Chinese area are only around 100 yuan, but the electricity prices are more expensive than in the concessions. (2) The concessions build roads, and many of them are built to the Chinese area, but the construction of roads in the Chinese area is slow. (3) The government should find ways to protect factories and shops in the Chinese area, and not allow any destructive actions, and eliminate excessive taxes and miscellaneous taxes and various bad habits. If this matter can be resolved, not only will factories in the concessions move back one after another, but also residents in the Chinese area will be more numerous. Various industries will develop as a result, and the market will flourish and revitalize day by day. The matter concerns the revitalization of the market and the development of industry, and it is reasonable to report the situation and request that your government review it and decide to implement it for the public convenience.

The Ministry of Finance Replied to the Chamber of Commerce that the Import of Coconut Oil Will Not Be Subject to Tax Reduction 126

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting a reduction in the import tax on coconut oil to reduce the cost of manufacturing domestic soap. The original text has been recorded in previous reports. It is learned that the Ministry of Finance replied to the Chamber of Commerce yesterday: Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the telegram has been received and understood. The case for the Chinese Soap Industry Association requesting that the customs duty on coconut oil used for manufacturing soap be reduced by half has been reviewed by the National Tariff System Committee. The Ministry has re-examined that the tax rate for coconut oil in the current import tariff is 2.70 gold units per picul, which is based on the tariff of 20 years ago and has not increased. The actual percentage rate now levied is higher than before due to the fall in the price of goods. Generally, after the tax rate is set, the percentage rate is small when the price of goods rises, and the percentage rate is high when the price of goods falls. This is the situation that should exist for ad valorem tax rates. Although the percentage rate of coconut oil actually levied has increased, the amount of tax payable per picul has not increased in the slightest. Even manufacturers who use this kind of falling-price raw material will only benefit and not be harmed. Moreover, the investigation shows that the coconut oil used to manufacture soap accounts for only a small part of its raw materials, and the import of foreign soap has gradually decreased in recent years, which proves that the industry has not been affected by this. The request to reduce the import tariff on coconut oil by half is difficult to approve. Please inform the industry accordingly. Winter Seal of the Ministry of Finance.

Implemented from April 10

The Shanghai National Products Road Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe Long-Distance Bus Company in this city has spent more than 500,000 yuan on purchasing land and building roads, which has been very painstaking. Recently, it has unified new cars and repaired the road surface, which has been praised by passengers. Now, to facilitate long-distance passengers, it has negotiated a joint transportation agreement between Pinghu and Shanghai with the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway Bureau, which will be implemented from April 10.
